The Fujian Students' Association in Beijing Asks for a Swift Resolution of the Fujian Affair: They Also Urge Li and Chen to Retreat from the Brink 88

Beijing News: The Fujian Students' Association in Beijing heard some time ago that there would be changes in Fujian. Zhang Yin, Wu Delu, Guo Zhaopi, Chen Dayuan, Lin Hao, Zhang Bo, Chen Lei and other executive directors and directors of the association, sent a telegram to the Fujian political and military authorities, advising them to put the overall situation first and not make changes. Recently, Fujian Province has established a government and declared independence. In addition to separately submitting reports to the National Government, the Executive Yuan, and the Military Commission to swiftly resolve the situation as soon as possible and save the people of Fujian from misery, they have also sent a telegram to Li Jishen and Chen Mingshu, urging them to retreat from the brink. The texts of the telegrams and reports are as follows:

(1) The text of the telegram to Li Chen et al. reads, "The Fujian Provincial Government in Fuzhou, addressed to Mr. Li Renchao, Chen Zhenru, Jiang Jingran, and Cai Xianchu, we are shocked to read in the newspapers that Fujian has established a government and declared independence. Our Fujian is plagued by bandits and communists, and powerful Japan is watching closely. Once something happens, it will inevitably become more rampant. Moreover, Fujian is poor and barren, and in recent years, the supplies have been exhausted. There is nowhere to increase the burden. Furthermore, your army's glorious resistance to Japan and its oath not to participate in civil wars are admired by the whole country, and you should not make any differences to lose credibility. We urge you to retreat from the brink and abolish the organization in order to avoid ruining the region and burdening the people of Fujian. We respectfully kowtow. Fujian Students' Association in Beijing, Executive Directors Zhang Yin, Wu Delu, Guo Zhaopi, et al." (2) The report to the National Government, the Executive Yuan, and the Military Commission reads, "Report requesting swift resolution of Chen Mingshu's and others' rebellion and disaster in Fujian to save the people of Fujian from misery. Our Fujian has suffered from corrupt politics and bandit disasters in recent years. The region is devastated, and the people are in dire straits. Last year, the 19th Route Army entered Fujian, and the provincial government was reorganized. We celebrated that someone was responsible and that suppression and governance could be expected. However, after more than a year, the governance performance was not evident, and the sound of extortion was constant. However, the people of Fujian still believed that the military expenses were urgent and tried to supply them, hoping that the 19th Route Army, which has the glory of resisting Japan, would not harm us. Recently, we read in the newspapers that the leaders of the 19th Route Army, Chen Mingshu and others, colluded with reactionary elements and frustrated politicians to organize a so-called People's Government in Fujian to resist the Central Government. Upon hearing this, we were shocked. Fujian is poor and has reached its limit. Regular political expenses and military salaries still need to rely on the assistance of the Central Government and Guangdong Province. Now that they have established their own government, set up agencies, and expanded military preparations, the expenses will be even greater. They will inevitably exhaust the pond to catch fish and dig the marrow to pay tribute. The people of Fujian are exhausted and impoverished, how can they bear it? This is the first way in which Chen Mingshu and others' rebellion will destroy the people's livelihood. Bandits and communists are everywhere in Fujian, and it is difficult to suppress them. The 19th Route Army has been suppressing them for more than a year, but they have not achieved any success in eliminating them. They have even resorted to recruiting bandits, which shows that their skills are exhausted. Recently, they have gone against the grain and accommodated the communists, announcing that land is owned by the public in order to win the favor of leftists. If they disrupt the order of Fujian and destroy the social organization in this way, it is unlikely that Fujian will not become a red zone like Jiangxi Province. This is the second way in which Chen Mingshu and others' rebellion will fuel the flames of the bandits. Moreover, Fujian is adjacent to Taiwan, and the Japanese have coveted it for a long time. Once something happens in Fujian, they may take the opportunity to start a war under the pretext of protecting overseas Chinese, or they may secretly manipulate and aid the chaos. If any of these things happen, Fujian will be in danger. We believe that internal pacification and external resistance are the established policies of the Central Government, and that unnecessary sacrifices should be avoided in order to avoid damaging the country's vitality. If the Japanese invaders are attracted to Fujian by this Fujian upheaval and repeat the mistakes of the Eastern Provinces, then we will not have control of Fujian, and the southeastern provinces will also be in danger. This is the third way in which Chen Mingshu and others' rebellion will attract the Japanese invaders. All of these points are of great importance to the situation in Fujian and the country. If they are not dealt with swiftly and resolved as soon as possible, the situation will expand and cause endless harm. We, the members of this association, are citizens of Fujian and dare not remain silent about what we see as dangerous. Therefore, we respectfully submit this report to your court, requesting you to swiftly resolve the situation as soon as possible and save the people of Fujian from misery. We are eagerly awaiting orders. Sincerely submitted."

Each Mongolian Banner Will Organize District Governments; Inner Mongolia's Autonomy Issue Is Completely Resolved; De Wang Abandoned His Claim for High Degree of Autonomy 89

Suiyuan Correspondence: The Inner Mongolia issue, after Huang Shaohong and Zhao Pilian stayed in Bailingmiao for a week and held multiple talks with De Wang and others, and through the mediation of the Panchen Lama and A Wang, finally reached a result on the night of November 17th. Huang, Zhao, and their entourage left Bailingmiao on the 19th to return to Suiyuan. Liu Puchen, specially dispatched by the General Staff Headquarters to accompany Huang and Zhao to Bailingmiao for inspection on the 18th, returned to Suiyuan from Bailingmiao ahead of them, accompanied by Huang's secretary, Zhuo Hongmou, and several members of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission's envoy, Ba Wenjun. Zhuo Hongmou was seriously injured in Bailingmiao on the 17th when his car overturned on the way to Yun Wang's residence, and he vomited blood on the spot. After a brief stop in Suiyuan, he left for Ping for medical treatment on the 19th. Liu Puchen, Ba Wenjun, and others stayed at the Suiyuan Hotel. Liu talked about the Bailingmiao meeting in detail, and a brief record is as follows: "After Huang, Zhao, and their party arrived in Bailingmiao, apart from banquets and other social engagements, no formal meetings were held. De Wang and Huang held meetings several times, but without concrete results, because Huang insisted on implementing the central government's plan, organizing the Mongolian Banner Political Committee, and establishing a closer relationship with the local government. De Wang insisted on organizing the Inner Mongolia Autonomous Government and refused to concede. Huang repeatedly expressed his intention to return to Suiyuan, but was persuaded to stay several times without success. Until the evening of the 17th, there were still no concrete results. Huang and Zhao decided to leave Bailingmiao on the 18th to return to Suiyuan no matter what. Through the mediation of the Panchen Lama, De Wang resolutely abandoned his consistent position late at night and asked the Panchen Lama to persuade Huang to stay in Bailingmiao for one more day. It was generally decided that the organization of the Inner Mongolia Autonomous Government would no longer be discussed. In the future, Mongolian Banner Autonomous Region governments will be established separately, identified by numbers, such as the First, Second, and Third Districts, etc. The organization of the district government and its contact with the local government were decided in principle. De Wang then presented a written statement to Huang, and Huang agreed to stay in Bailingmiao for one more day on the 18th to discuss the detailed methods. At this point, the Inner Mongolia Autonomous Government issue, which had caused a great uproar, came to an end and can be said to be completely resolved. Huang and Zhao spent their last day in Bailingmiao on the 18th, conducting research and engaging in social activities simultaneously. With their mission accomplished, they decided to leave Bailingmiao on the 19th to return to Suiyuan." Liu also said that on the Inner Mongolia autonomy issue, most people do not understand this move by the Mongolian compatriots. In fact, self-defense is a human instinct. Three provinces have fallen, Rehe has also been lost, and eastern Mongolia is gone. Western Mongolia must accumulate strength to rescue itself, protect the territory, and secure the borders. The Mongolian compatriots, in view of this situation, rose up and urgently sought self-help. We should absolutely sympathize with them, but the methods need to be studied further. Through the inspection of Minister Huang and Vice-Chairman Zhao, the central government and Inner Mongolia have established close ties. From now on, the whole country, from top to bottom, will pay attention to Mongolia, work hard to manage it, consolidate the borders, and strengthen national defense. It may not be that this incident has promoted it, etc. (18th)

Changsha's Bond-Raising Craze; Key Figures in Various Industries Arrested; He Yuanwen Accuses Merchants of Being Reactionary; Those Arrested Escorted to Pingxiang; Municipal Chamber of Commerce Pleads with He Jian for Their Release 90

Changsha Correspondence: Hunan Province issued 5 million yuan of national salvation bonds. The Changsha business community was assigned 360,000 yuan based on operating capital, which was later reduced to 60% of that, or 210,000 yuan. Because the merchants only paid 46,000 yuan and were delayed in paying the full amount, the provincial government sent soldiers to strictly urge payment from house to house. Except for the money, silk, and gold industries with strong capital, which directly negotiated with the provincial government and paid 9,000 yuan first to get the soldiers withdrawn, the other industries believed that the distribution of public debt was uneven. On the 16th, they held a joint secret meeting and decided on six measures, the most important of which were: (1) To organize a temporary office for various industries to oppose the extra levy of national salvation bonds, and to elect Cui Bohong, chairman of the pigment industry, Huang Juqiao of the pharmaceutical industry, Yuan Yousheng, chairman of the paper industry, Chen Lanshu, chairman of the dry goods industry, Xu Tianxi, chairman of the dyeing industry, Li Dongxian, chairman of the oil industry, Yu Jianfan, chairman of the oil, salt, cotton, and yarn industry, Wei Lansheng, chairman of the book industry, Wei Guisong, chairman of the Jiangsu and Guangdong goods industry, Huang Boxun, chairman of the hardware industry, and Wang Boqing, chairman of the rice industry, to be responsible for everything. (2) If the provincial government arrests people to forcibly collect national salvation bonds, all businesses will go on strike. (3) If any industry undermines the united movement and independently subscribes to public bonds, they will be punished. (4) Print slogans with the wording "This store is unable to pay extra national salvation bonds and will cease operations," and prepare to post them at the doors of each store during the strike. The situation was extremely tense. Later, Zhang Kailian, Director of the Finance Department, and Zuo Yizhai and Wang Pinxin, standing committee members of the Changsha Municipal Chamber of Commerce, convened a joint meeting of all executive and supervisory committee members on the afternoon of the 17th and decided on two measures: (1) Request the government to withdraw the soldiers first. All unpaid public debt will be negotiated and handled by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce with the government. (2) Request the industry guilds to suspend the prepared strike resolution and wait for the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to resolve it. As a result, the soldiers who were sitting in the stores urging payment on the 18th were withdrawn, and the strike trend had eased. Unexpectedly, He Yuanwen, the mayor of Changsha in charge of raising public bonds, rushed to Pingxiang on the 17th and secretly reported to He Jian that Changsha merchants, incited by reactionaries, were planning to use the issue of raising public bonds to carry out a strike in order to disrupt the rear. He immediately telegraphed Hu Da, commander of the Provincial Garrison Command, to arrest the eleven people in charge of the temporary offices of various industries and escort them to Pingxiang for investigation. After Hu received the order, he invited the eleven people to the headquarters for a talk early on the 18th. Only Huang Juqiao, Cui Bohong, Yuan Yousheng, Xu Tianxi, Yu Jianfan, Li Dongxian, Chen Lanshu, and Wei Guisong arrived at the headquarters at that time. Except for Wei Guisong, who was released on bail due to illness, the other seven people were immediately escorted to the headquarters of the Western Route General Headquarters in Pingxiang and held in solitary confinement, treated as bandits who disrupted public order, and were not allowed to communicate or meet with anyone. At the same time, officials were sent to inform the newspapers, instructing them not to publish news about this case. Troops were also dispatched to arrest the three who had not been arrested, Wei Lansheng, Wu Boxun, and Wang Boqing. The city was in a state of panic, and the merchants were especially uneasy. On the day the chairmen of various industries were escorted to Pingxiang, He Jian happened to return to the province from Pingxiang. Zuo Yizhai, a standing committee member of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and key figures from the Provincial Government and Provincial Party Headquarters went to pay their respects and inquire about the matter. He said that they were instigated by bad people to disrupt the rear of Changsha, printed slogans, and incited strikes, which was indeed conclusive evidence and must be severely punished. Zuo and others tried their best to explain, saying that although their words and texts were careless, they were not being used by others to plot against the government and pleaded for leniency. However, He Jian, in his anger, insisted on severe punishment, so there was no result. On the 20th, He Jian also explained the matter in an expanded memorial week report, saying that the army was fighting bandits on the front line, but the reactionaries were disrupting the rear, which was deeply hated and must be strictly punished according to law. As a result, the situation became more serious. On the 21st, various industries in Changsha held a meeting in the city and provincial capital to discuss rescue measures. It was decided that Zuo Yizhai and Wang Pinxin would present a statement to He Jian to explain the misunderstanding and prove that the arrested chairmen and committee members had not committed any illegal acts, and acknowledged that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce would be responsible for overall planning regarding the issue of raising public bonds in the future. At the same time, Zhang Kailian and others also tried their best to intercede with He Jian, so that the arrested people might not be in any danger. However, the written statement from various industries was submitted to He Jian on the evening of the 21st, but He had already left Changsha at 3 pm that afternoon. When He will return is still unknown. The outcome of this case will not be known until He returns to the province. (November 22nd)

Xuzhou: Paper Money Panic Gradually Subsides; Business Still Depressed; Finance Still Panicked 91

Xuzhou Correspondence: The Xuzhou private paper money panic has gradually subsided. The establishment of the Public Exchange Office was originally intended to help the poor, but gathering all the companies in one place with a large number of people led to repeated tragedies. Since yesterday (the 23rd), Gongyu, Shixingchang, and Tianbaoyu have begun to redeem their own paper money. Gongyu has obtained a loan of 20,000 yuan from the banking community by discounting from reliable shareholders to maintain the redemption, while the liquidation office is still handling the liquidation. The redeemed paper money is sealed up daily. Shixingchang and Tianbaoyu are solely owned by private individuals who circulate cash on their own to maintain the current redemption, and they also seal up the paper money as they redeem it. Bu Xinji, Chunquan, Yizhenxiang, and Juhechang are still redeeming their paper money at the Public Exchange Office. Once each company has raised cash, they will withdraw from the Public Exchange Office separately and redeem their own paper money. However, the situation of public and private redemption at each company is still very crowded, but the number of people has been slightly dispersed, so that tragedies will not occur again.

The Money Ticket Cleaning Committee established by the county government will thoroughly clean up private money tickets. Each ticket has been observing the situation, planning to maintain the current trend in the past, and thinking about continuing to issue them in order to make a comeback. Some are also aware of their emptiness and have privately misappropriated account assets and industries, planning to settle the matter with a collapse. People in the society have now understood everything and are determined to maintain a permanent ban and thorough compensation. If their property is insufficient, they are determined to demand severe punishment by law. Therefore, private tickets have now become a dead end. The ticket merchants, who have been criticized by the society, have also been unable to come up with a solution. However, whether the subsequent step-by-step implementation will be able to persist depends on the political parties and authorities.

At present, the market is inconsistent in its use or rejection of various tickets. Large stores avoid trouble and refuse to use them all together. Small businesses will either stop operating without them, or use them reluctantly, with discounts of 20% or 10%, which is extremely chaotic. The depression of business and the panic of finance have both plummeted. It is feared that the situation will be even more unbearable by the end of the year. (24th)

Ancient Tomb of the Ming Dynasty in Songjiang Is Looted 92

In the deserted mounds of Caojiajing in Xinqu District 20, there is the tomb of Li Jingjiang, a famous general of the Ming Dynasty, which has been around for more than 500 years. Unexpectedly, Xia Damazi (also known as Zaiqin) from Yancheng hired many workers at the beginning of this month to excavate it. A total of nine coffins made of Phoebe nanmu were dug up, and each one was opened. The corpses were all intact, but they decayed immediately after being exposed to the wind. Jade and porcelain burial objects were looted and disappeared immediately. The local people learned about the incident and suspected that Zhang Wanyao, the district chief of the area, had instigated it, and filed complaints with the party and government agencies. The county government has sent personnel to investigate the case. Xia Damazi, who was at large, has been captured by Hua Wenren, a patrol officer from the 10th police station in Xinqiao, and transferred to the prosecutor's office of the county court for interrogation and detention.

Parricidal Son in Jiaodiaowan 93

Wang Xianglong, a villager from Linglou, Jiaodiaowan, had two sons, Yuelou and Xinglou, who were both married, and a married daughter. On the 20th of this month, they split the family property and lived separately. On the 23rd, his daughter returned to Ning to visit. At night, the old father was preparing the bed for his daughter and asked his eldest daughter-in-law for a mosquito net. The daughter-in-law refused to give it, which caused an argument. Unexpectedly, the eldest son did not persuade them to stop, but joined in the whirlpool and struck his father with farm tools, injuring his head and waist, causing his father to die under the stick. The situation was very tragic. The second son, Xinglou, was filled with grief and indignation and petitioned the court to seek justice. On the 25th, a prosecutor supervised the coroner and police to conduct an examination.

Bizarre Details of Murder Case in Jiaozhi, Suzhou 94

The murder case in Xishi, Jiaozhi Town, under the jurisdiction of Wukun County, is extremely tragic. The local court dispatched prosecutor Lu Wenqin, clerk Chen Penggeng, and coroner Xuan Fang to the countryside on the 24th to conduct an investigation. They felt that although the clues to this case were difficult to obtain quickly, there were several points worth studying. (1) Zhou, the mother of the deceased Ma Fushou, had already divided the property and awarded it to the deceased and her son-in-law Lu Fusheng. She herself was supported by her son Fushou and son-in-law Fusheng in rotation every five days. On the night of the incident, Zhou originally lived in her son's house and was invited to Zhang's wedding feast by her son-in-law. (2) When the property was divided in the 19th year, her son received sixteen mu of land, and her son-in-law only received eight mu of land on the surface. However, it was heard that Zhou had a total of more than one hundred mu of land, not including private savings, and her son-in-law Lu Fusheng built a huge new house in Xiatang after receiving the land, which neighbors discussed a lot. (3) Zhou's bedroom contained land deeds, silver dollars, and newly purchased clothing. Zhou did not lock the door of the room on the night of the incident. (4) If this case was a robbery, why was no property lost in the deceased's room? (5) If it was a case of adultery and jealousy, it would have been enough to kill Wang alone. The local court is currently investigating.

Zhenjiang Yangzhong County Residents Resist Taxes and Riot 95

Yangzhong County is isolated in the middle of the river, with barren land and poor people, and strong folk customs. Wuxi Taixin Silk Factory Fire 96

The Taixin Silk Factory (the original site of the Yuanyou Silk Factory) near Changfeng Bridge on Guangqin Road, which had a total of 244 silk machines, was managed by Xu Junjie and assisted by Cheng Yinxiang. It started operating on September 1st of this year. Due to the tragic fall in the silk market, it suffered heavy losses. The factory had insured more than 10,000 taels of fire insurance with the Anding Insurance Company. Yesterday (the 25th) at about 1:00 AM, a fire suddenly broke out in the factory's dried cocoon warehouse, causing a conflagration. Thick smoke filled the air, and flames shot out in all directions. Before long, it broke through the roof and was approaching the surroundings. When it was noticed, gongs were sounded to warn the neighborhood, and fire brigades from inside and outside the city rushed to the scene to put out the fire. As a result, 236 packages of dried cocoons, 10 packages of double palace cocoons, 14 packages of printed head rotten cocoons, 3 packages of cocoon clothing, 10 packages of long silk were burned, and four houses were destroyed, with a total loss of more than 10,000 yuan. The cause of the fire is still under investigation.

Yangzhou Rice Noodles Contain Poison, Nearly Killing Fourteen People 97

Yin Guomin, a village guard from Shijia Garden, Shaobo South Township, borrowed a liter of rice noodles from his neighbor Wang Yaoshan, and then returned them. The Wang family made dumplings with them for the whole family's dinner. Unexpectedly, about an hour after eating, all seven members of the family suffered from headaches, abdominal pain, vomiting, and other symptoms of poisoning. The next morning, they negotiated with the Yin family. Yin also used the noodles to make pancakes for his whole family to eat. One after another, the same symptoms appeared as in the Wang family. The situation was very dangerous. It is said that a total of fourteen people from both families were victims and were taken to Shaobo Town for emergency medical treatment. Fortunately, they have escaped danger. Whether the rice noodles contain poison is currently being studied and tested.

Kong Xiangxi Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday, Said Fujian Customs Revenue Has Not Been Robbed; Candidates to Welcome Hu Still Undecided 101

Tragedy at Changzhou Station on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Yesterday Afternoon; Five Soldiers and Passengers Killed or Injured Due to Hand Grenade Explosion 102

At 1:20 yesterday afternoon, when the seventh express train arrived at Changzhou Station on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, a soldier guarding the railway exploded a hand grenade when the rope broke and it fell to the ground. One passenger and one soldier were killed on the spot, and one passenger and two soldiers were injured. The details are recorded below.

Soldiers Disembarking: More than 100 soldiers from the 4th company, 1st battalion, 523rd regiment, 362nd brigade, 88th division, commanded by Company Commander Cao Yingben, were ordered to transfer from Gaozi Station to Changzhou to guard the railway. Company Commander Cao led the team yesterday morning and set off on the 7th express train on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, arriving at Changzhou at 1:20 pm. They disembarked at the front end of the north platform.

Grenade Explosion: At that time, a soldier exploded a hand grenade when the rope he was wearing broke and it suddenly fell to the ground. There was great chaos at the time. Zhong Jianhuai, the chief of the Changzhou police section of the railway, supervised and led the railway police to maintain order.

Casualties: After the investigation, it was found that two soldiers were injured. Sun Bohe, a second-class passenger from Zhenjiang to Shanghai and an employee of the Shanghai Bank, was injured in both legs. Hua Zhushan, a third-class passenger from Zhenjiang to Shanghai and an employee of Zhenjiang Fukang, died of serious injuries. Both passengers got off the train to take a walk on the platform because they felt bored in the car, and were caught in the disaster.

Aftermath: The injured soldiers were handled by Company Commander Cao himself. The injured passenger Sun Bohe was given emergency surgery by the station doctor Gong and then sent to Wujin Hospital for treatment. The station chief telegraphed Zhenjiang to visit the family of the deceased passenger Hua Zhushan and come to Changzhou to handle the matter.

Train Continued: At the same time, three glass windows of the 605th second-class passenger car were also shattered by the explosion, but fortunately no passengers in the car were injured. The 7th express train left Changzhou as usual.

Ningjing Ship Ran Aground in Huangshi Port; Ship Has Been Flooded Six Feet; Company Sends Personnel to Rescue 103

The Changjiang wheel steamer Ningjing of the Ningshao Company, which was loading cargo from Hankou back to Shanghai yesterday, suddenly ran aground while traveling near Huangshi Port. The ship has been flooded six feet. The company has now sent personnel to rescue. The details are as follows:

Ran Aground Yesterday Morning 104

The Ningjing ship set off from Hankou in the middle of the night on the 24th and sailed downstream to Shanghai. Yesterday at dawn, the ship was at a river surface 68 miles away from Huangshi Port near Jiujiang. Due to foggy weather, the pilot was careless, causing the ship to hit an underwater reef, breaking the bottom of the Ningjing ship and immediately flooding it.

Unable to Escape 105

After the Ningjing ship had an accident, the shipowner, Russian Gao Zilofu A. Kosloff, and the first and second mates Shi Junxin and Zhang Hai, immediately tried their best to find a way to escape the danger, but the ship was trapped in the reef, and after repeatedly starting the car, they could not drive away from the reef beach, and the river water poured into the ship wildly.

Cargo Hold Flooded 106

The Ningjing ship was loaded with more than 8,300 dan of goods, which were loaded in various cabins. After running aground, the shipowner sent a telegram to Shanghai to report to the company for rescue at 11:00 AM. Sent Personnel to Inspect 107

After receiving the news, the company felt that the matter was urgent and needed to be rescued immediately. After the company discussed, it immediately entrusted Hengchangxiang to assign technicians to rush to the scene of the accident for inspection in order to provide rescue.

Ningshao Went to Rescue 108

The Ningshao Company decided to send the old Ningshao ship to fly to Huangshi Port to load and transport cargo and seek rescue, but the Ningshao ship was rented by the Transportation Department. That night, the company telegraphed the Transportation Department to negotiate the release so that it could go to the rescue, but it had not been resolved late at night.

Insurance of 200,000 109

The Ningjing ship has a deadweight of more than 2,000 tons. The company purchased it a few years ago. The ship hull is insured for a total of 200,000 yuan. The ship's comprador is Zhang Yunquan, and there are a total of 47 crew members, 24 sailors and stokers, and 16 business personnel.

Cotton Mills Buying Cotton - Exemption from Business Tax Approved - Ministry of Finance Considers Business Difficulties and Relieves Cotton Industry - Cotton Industry Control Committee's Letter to the Factory Association for Reference 111

Cotton mills setting up stations in producing areas to purchase cotton had previously been granted an exemption from business tax by the Ministry of Finance out of consideration for the difficulties faced by businesses. This has been implemented in various provinces for some time. In Jiangsu Province, however, due to the lack of clear understanding by various business tax bureaus, there were instances where cotton purchasing stations were ordered to pay business tax. After reports were submitted by various factories to the National Economic Commission, the commission sent letters to both the ministry and the provincial government for consultation. It is now reported that a satisfactory resolution has been reached. Business tax bureaus in Jiangsu Province will no longer levy business tax on cotton purchasing stations established by cotton mills in cotton-producing areas. The original letter from the Cotton Industry Control Committee to the Cotton Mill Association is as follows: "Respectfully, we have repeatedly received letters reporting that Qingfeng, Shenxin, Yongan, Yukang, and other factories'

Cotton Purchasing in Various Locations 112

stations are being forced to pay taxes or having goods confiscated by business tax bureaus, and requesting measures to stop this. After this association separately sent letters to relevant authorities to instruct them to stop such practices, we also sent representatives to Beijing to present the situation to the Ministry of Finance and urge them to quickly formulate preventative measures. Now, we have received a reply from these representatives stating that the Ministry of Finance's policy regarding the exemption of cotton purchasing stations from business tax has been followed in provinces such as Hubei, Henan, Anhui, Shandong, Shanxi, and Chahar since the promulgation of the order. Previously, Jiangsu Province, based on Article 20 of the Business Tax Regulations, requested the Ministry to apply a different measure. However, because the matter concerned a general case, it was deemed inappropriate to treat Jiangsu Province differently. After detailed explanation, it was replied on the 20th of this month that the established method of exempting cotton purchasing stations from business tax should still be followed. Subsequent disputes should thus be resolved. Furthermore, we received a letter from the Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance stating that the matter of cotton mills establishing purchasing stations in cotton-producing areas to purchase cotton for raw materials could not be exempted from tax due to existing regulations. Now, upon receiving an order from the Ministry of Finance, it has been decided that

Scope of Exemption 113

is limited to the raw materials used by the factory itself and should be followed accordingly. All bureaus have been notified to comply and detailed procedures for inspection, verification, and the issuance of tax exemption notices have been established. Cotton mills that need to send personnel to cotton-producing areas to purchase raw cotton should first report the required quantity to the business tax bureau in the location of the main factory, fill out a tax exemption form, and notify the business tax bureau in the cotton-producing area for inspection and verification to release the goods. When the raw cotton is transported back to the factory, the first part of the tax exemption form should be returned to the business tax bureau in the location of the main factory for verification. The registration licenses of the main factory and branch offices should also be sent to the bureau for inspection to comply with regulations. While every effort should be made to protect the raw materials used by cotton mills, strict precautions should also be taken to prevent shadow companies from exploiting loopholes and evading taxes, so as not to affect tax revenue and give rise to criticism. We hope that you will forward this to the cotton mills to follow the prescribed procedures, carry out the process in a responsible way, and supervise each other to prevent misuse by others, so that both the factories and tax authorities can benefit. We hereby send this letter to you, and we hope that you will inform the factories to take note and comply. This is addressed to the Chinese Cotton Mill Association."

Japanese Ships Issue New Regulations - Suppressing Chinese Entry - Guarantee Deposit Increased to 100 Japanese Yen 114

Since the January 28th Incident, many Chinese who had returned home now intended to return to Shanghai to resume their businesses. In recent months, the number of people traveling from Shanghai to Japan has increased, mostly laborers and those involved in trades like barbering, kimono shops, and restaurants. Several dozen groups have been barred from entry. The Japanese have now gone a step further and issued new regulations to suppress this, which have been implemented since yesterday, making it even more difficult for Chinese to travel to Japan. The situation is described as follows:

Increased Deposit 115

In the past, Chinese traveling to Japan, such as those traveling in third class, had to pay a deposit of 30 yuan before departure. If they were denied entry, this amount would be deducted to cover travel expenses. Because the number of Chinese traveling to Japan has increased, and there are deportations and expulsions on nearly every ship, the Japanese Postal Steamship Company sent a telegram to Shanghai yesterday stating that, starting on the 25th of this month, regardless of whether Chinese traveling to Japan have passports or certificates, all third-class passengers and those seeking work in Japan must pay an increased deposit of 100 Japanese yen before purchasing a ticket, for which the shipping company will issue a receipt. If they are allowed to land in Japan, they can reclaim the deposit with the receipt. Without this amount, no ticket will be sold.

Shanghai Companies Implement 116

Local Japanese shipping companies have already complied with the new regulations and increased the deposit for passengers traveling to Japan. At 10:00 AM yesterday, a group of seven or eight Chinese planning to travel to Kobe and other places in Japan went to a Japanese shipping company to purchase tickets. They each paid the deposit of 30 yuan, but the Japanese shipping company presented the new regulations, requiring them to pay an additional 100 yen. The Chinese passengers did not have such a large amount of money at the time. After repeated negotiations, they were unable to come to an agreement, and they had to leave. The reporter later inquired with these passengers, who stated that they had been recruited by Chinese-owned restaurants, kimono shops, and other businesses in Japan. Their travel expenses had been pieced together with difficulty. They asked where they could get such a large deposit. From now on, Chinese traveling to Japan can only sigh in despair at the vast ocean.

Encountered Danger in Zhoushan the Day Before Yesterday - Sikorsky Plane Disassembled and Transported to Shanghai - No One Seriously Injured - Minimal Mail Loss, Currently Being Sorted - Next Shanghai-Guangdong Flight Will Depart as Scheduled 124

Guowen News Agency reports that the China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Guangdong flight reported to the Shanghai head office at 8:35 AM on the 24th that the weather was poor and would return to Shanghai. The company speculated that the southbound plane would return to Shanghai after sending the message. Unexpectedly, when the plane was turning north, it hit an island peak due to heavy fog. However, according to many passengers, if it were not for the superb skills and quick thinking of pilot Lumir, the passengers and pilots on the plane would not have survived.

Rescue Situation 125

After the plane was damaged, pilot Lumir disregarded his own injuries and immediately assisted the passengers in leaving the plane to find a safe place. Together with the local people and the mass forces of the defense team, they chartered a boat to transport the passengers, mail, and luggage back to Shanghai.

Flight Schedule Unchanged 126

The company's Shanghai-Guangdong route was originally scheduled to run twice a week. The company has decided to maintain the original schedule, and the next southbound flight will depart as scheduled next Tuesday (November 28). Although there is only one Sikorsky plane, there are two spare engines for timely replacement. Therefore, the current situation can still be maintained continuously. The company is also using the Loening amphibian as a backup plane to ensure that the flight schedule is not interrupted by this accident.

New Plane to Fill the Gap 127

For the time being, the company will have a new plane shipped from the United States to fill the gap. In about a few months, the Shanghai-Guangdong route will also purchase newer, faster planes that are faster than the Sikorsky. This will reduce the round trip time between Shanghai and Guangdong to two days, instead of the current three. At that time, the flight schedule will be changed to three times a week. In the spring and summer, the Sikorsky plane can reach Shanghai and Guangdong in two days for a round trip. Currently, it is winter, the days are short, and the northbound plane often encounters northerly headwinds, so the northbound plane cannot reach Shanghai on the same day after taking off from Guangzhou.

Next Passengers 128

Next month, construction will begin on a larger hangar at Longhua to accommodate the new, fast planes for the Shanghai-Chongqing route. These planes will arrive in Shanghai soon. There will be seven passengers on the southbound Shanghai-Guangdong flight next Tuesday, and two passengers from Guangzhou, two from Shantou, and one from Fuzhou on the northbound flight on Wednesday.

Dispatching a Boat to Tow the Plane 129

The China National Aviation Corporation hired a small boat from Wheelock, Marden & Co. yesterday to sail to Caiqi Mountain in Haiyan to tow the damaged Sikorsky No. 16 to Shanghai for repairs.

Recalling the Accident 130

According to passengers who witnessed the accident yesterday, the plane took off at 6:05 AM on the 24th and turned back to Shanghai due to fog. It took off again at 8:20 AM. There was no fog within about 20 miles of Longhua Airport, but the clouds were low. Because the clouds were low, the plane could not fly high. Looking down at the sea, the seawater was yellow. After flying forward for about 20 miles, it suddenly encountered fog again, which was also yellow. The sky and the water were the same color. The pilot could not fly forward, so he telegraphed Longhua Airport to say that he would turn back and turned the plane around to return. At that time, the speed of the plane had been reduced from 110 miles per hour to 60 miles per hour. Just as it was turning around, a strange peak suddenly appeared, vaguely visible in the fog, about 270 feet high. It was already too late to avoid it. The pilot raised the nose of the plane and went straight up into the clouds, but he did not rise high enough. The bottom of the plane eventually touched down on the mountainside of Caiqi Mountain. Fortunately, the fuel was shut off, but the plane still rushed forward for about 100 yards before flipping over and stopping. Therefore, everyone suffered minor injuries. If the plane had flipped over as soon as it landed, it would have been unthinkable. The site was about 200 feet above sea level. The plane's wings had been destroyed, the engine was slightly damaged, but the fuselage was undamaged.

Pilot's Experience 131

It is heard that the pilot Lumir had 5,000 hours of flying experience, so he was able to remove the seaplane wheels and shut off the fuel at the critical moment. Otherwise, the plane would have caught fire, and all nine people on board would have perished.

Injuries of Each Person 132

The injured people who were transported from Zhapu twice at 11:00 PM and 1:30 AM the night before were all sent to Hong En Hospital for treatment. The injuries were as follows: (1) Co-pilot Aimar, both ankles were broken, so the injury was the most serious; (2) Lady Keelis (niece of British Minister Lampson), both ankles were broken and there were abrasions; (3) US Consul in Fuzhou, Reynolds, leg injuries and minor abrasions; (4) Xu Bojian of Asiatic Electric Company, leg injury and abrasions; (5) Zhang Shunfan, manager of Fuzhou Motor Company, leg injuries and abrasions; (6) Yang Mingxin, Superintendent of Wenzhou Customs, leg injury; (7) Yang Zhonghe, back injury. The destinations of each person were Yang Mingxin and Yang Zhonghe to Wenzhou, Reynolds, Xu Bojian, and Zhang Shunfan to Fuzhou, and Lady Keelis to Hong Kong.

Two People Discharged 133

(1) The injuries of the main pilot Lumir were very minor. He was discharged yesterday after bandaging. (2) The injuries of Skavfer, a German from Kong Si Yanghang, were also minor. He was also discharged yesterday.

Mail Loss 134

According to a reporter from the Shenshi News Agency, the plane carried a total of 33 pounds of mail, including mail for Wenzhou, Fuzhou, Shantou, and other stations. After the accident, only the mail for Fuzhou was slightly damaged due to the mailbags being broken. A bag of mail bound for Guangzhou was also lost and is currently being searched for. Otherwise, most of the mail was unharmed. However, the company and the post office conducted a detailed inspection and handled them separately yesterday. They will still be transported and distributed as usual when the Guangdong-Shanghai plane goes south on the next flight.

Increase in Chinese Tea Exports in October - More Than 8,000 Dan Higher Than in the Same Month Last Year 135

Central News Agency reports that, according to the International Trade Bureau, a total of 39,944 dan and 34 jin of Chinese tea were exported in October of this year, which is more than 8,000 dan higher than in the same month last year. The largest increase was in exports to Russia, followed by exports to the United States and India. Exports to Britain and France decreased.

Shanghai County Government - Proclamation to Farmers to Pay Rent as Usual 137

The Shanghai County Government issued a proclamation yesterday stating, "Landowners rely on property to make a living, and tenant farmers rely on farming for food. They depend on each other for mutual benefit, and they each have the responsibility to pay taxes and rent. There is also a lot of mutual understanding. Although the districts under the county suffered from typhoons this year, the harvest is inevitably shorter. The total harvest is still not too far from the harvest in a good year. Landowners should not make unreasonable demands, and tenants should not arbitrarily reduce or discount the rent, or listen to rumors, wait and see, and cause trouble, which will lead to investigation. Everyone must abide by this."

At the Border Between the Chinese and Concession Areas - Water and Electricity Problems for Residents in the Chinese Area - Land Bureau Proclaims That Supply Should be Provided by the Chinese Area - Severe Punishment for Illegally Connecting to Concession Water and Electricity 138

The Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau proclaimed yesterday, "The Bureau has previously investigated cases where houses located at the border between the Chinese and concession areas, whose addresses are located in the Chinese area, often arbitrarily connect to water and electricity from the concessions, which greatly harms national sovereignty. A measure to ban this was drafted in September of the 18th year of the Republic, stipulating that residents at the border between the Chinese and concession areas whose residences are located entirely in the Chinese area must use water and electricity supplied by the Chinese area. Otherwise, once discovered, they will be ordered to dismantle the connection automatically and will be punished accordingly. If they refuse to comply, the houses will be sealed up. As for houses located at the border between the Chinese and concession areas that straddle both the Chinese and concession areas, residents who want to connect to water and electricity must first report their address and house number to the Bureau. The Bureau will instruct them to connect to water and electricity from which side, and the Bureau will present this measure to the Municipal Government for approval and proclamation to all residents at the border between the Chinese and concession areas. Recently, reports have indicated that residents at the border are still illegally connecting to water and electricity from the concessions, which is inappropriate. Now, in order to strictly enforce administrative orders and safeguard sovereignty, the Bureau, in addition to investigating and punishing residents who illegally connect to water and electricity from the concessions, hereby proclaims to all residents at the border to abide by the previous measure and not to arbitrarily connect to water and electricity from the concessions. This is the proclamation, signed by Director Xu Peihuang."

Zhang Zilian and Others Initiate the Organization of a Domestic Yarn Purchasing Agency - Issue Declaration 139

Since the January 28th Incident, there has been a consensus across all sectors to resist enemy goods and raw materials. However, for yarn, small cloth factories and knitting factories still purchase them separately. Zhang Zilian and others in the domestic goods sector, seeing this, invited textile tycoons such as Li Rongchu, Rong Moxian, Hu Peng, Dong Quesun, Wang Haoran, and Zheng Haiuo to jointly organize the China Domestic Yarn Purchasing Agency. They leased a three-story building at No. 19, South of Nanjing Road, Guizhou Road, as a business location. They have already signed special contracts with various Chinese yarn mills and have notified cloth factories, knitting factories, towel factories to purchase domestic yarn in the future and not to use enemy goods. It is heard that they will start business today. The agency's declaration states: "The dumping policy is the most poisonous trick that international capitalist countries use on small and weak nations. International capitalist countries know that small and weak nations cannot break free from their shackles in the contradictory economic phenomenon, so they satisfy their desire for high oppression and maintain their own lives. The consistent plan of imperialist Japan's aggression against China is to use the dumping policy as its goal. In order to achieve its poisonous plan, it must break our country's nascent industries, form a larger chaos, and accelerate the destruction of the country and the extinction of the race. The lost land of Liaodong has not been recovered, and the traces of the war in northern Shanghai are still there. Japanese yarn and thread are already invincible in the cotton textile industry. Small-scale cotton textile factories must rely on this to survive. Is this not a hopeless situation? The concept of individual interest dominates their actions, and treacherous merchants take the opportunity to deceive and lure them, disregarding the survival of the entire nation. These economic traitors created by the environment, although their stupidity is unparalleled, their feelings are actually excusable. We have been working in the cotton textile industry for more than ten years and know this situation well. Sitting and talking does not help the facts, only action can be effective. Therefore, we organized the China Domestic Yarn Purchasing Co., Ltd. at the south of Nanjing Road, Guizhou Road in Shanghai, concentrating all domestic yarn, offering the lowest prices, and striving to promote sales, so that goods have a destination, and treacherous people cannot mix fish eyes with pearls to achieve their deceitful and profitable schemes. Where justice lies, we will devote all our efforts to ensure that cotton textile factories use domestic yarn as much as possible, so that our country's textile industry will not be oppressed by the dumping strategy of Japanese imperialism and be on the verge of bankruptcy. Cotton textile factories can use pure domestic raw materials to create finished products for the people's needs, leaving a glimmer of hope for the national economy, so that we can get respite and restore. Furthermore, we will urge textile factories to improve their products and improve their economic organization, so that the economic relationship with cotton textile factories is coordinated and closely linked, and we will fight Japanese imperialism in the economic market. We know that our efforts are weak and we dare not be complacent. We swear to be sincere, work hard, and fight. Gentlemen of the nation, we hope that you will guide us forward. This is our declaration. We hope you will consider it."

Shanghai Municipal Statistics Published Yesterday 143

The Shanghai Local Association, considering Shanghai as the hub of East Asian transportation and that the success or failure of various undertakings is related to the whole country and the world, hired experts last October. After ten months of effort, they compiled the Shanghai Municipal Statistics. The contents are divided into sixteen categories: land, population, administration, justice, finance, banking, commerce, industry, labor, agriculture, transportation, public utilities, cultural undertakings, education, society, and hygiene. There are four hundred tables. Most of the materials were collected from public, private, Chinese, and foreign organizations and private individuals in the city, and some were obtained through on-site investigations. The data mainly pertains to 1932, with past materials covering the most recent three years, and some extending back more than ten years. Statistical experts, including Mr. Liu Dajun, Mr. Cai Zhengya, Mr. Zhang Xinyi, and Mr. Wu Zelin, provided guidance and design. Each category had several experts who carefully reviewed the data. Finally, Mr. Cai Zhengya conducted a final review. Therefore, the content is rich, the compilation is novel, the figures are accurate, and the printing is excellent. It can be used as a reference for legislation, administration, study, writing, and domestic and foreign trade, meeting various needs. Recognizing that Shanghai is a global metropolis attracting worldwide attention and that many foreigners desire to understand Shanghai's true situation, the association specially published the book in a Chinese-English bilingual format. The entire book contains more than four hundred pages and is bound into a large volume. It was published on the 25th. It is said that the association aims to serve society, and the price is very low: the paperback version costs silver $2.85, plus postage of $0.30; the hardcover version costs silver $3.85, plus postage of $0.30; and the hardcover international edition costs US$1.80, postage included. During the pre-publication reservation period, nearly a thousand copies were ordered from home and abroad. In addition to being distributed by the association (No. 1138 Jing'an Temple Road), it is also entrusted to be distributed by local newspapers, the Commercial Press, Life Bookstore, and the branches of both the Shen Bao and Commercial Press in various locations, as well as the special sales agents of Life Bookstore in various places.

Meeting Notes of the Yangzhong Native Place Industry and Commerce Association in Shanghai - Discussion of Ways to Deal with Land Tax 144

The Yangzhong Native Place Industry and Commerce Association in Shanghai, due to the Yangzhong County government's forced collection of land taxes on the 22nd of this month, which aroused public outrage and led to a major tragedy, convened a general meeting yesterday afternoon to discuss solutions. Chen Xiaoshan was elected chairman. The chairman first reported that the county is small, the people are poor, and the taxes are heavy. In recent years, disasters and crop failures have been frequent, and the rural areas are almost bankrupt. The people are struggling to survive and unanimously requested the county government to reduce land tax surcharges to allow them to survive. Because the surcharges exceed the regular tax by more than four times, the people cannot bear the burden. Recently, after the Executive Yuan and Ministry of Finance of the National Government, and Jiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the Military Council, successively issued telegrams to provinces and counties strictly prohibiting surcharges from exceeding the regular tax, the people's movement to reduce taxes became more concrete. However, the county government disregarded the regulations and the people's difficulties, insisting on forced collection, which aroused unrest and resulted in the loss of lives. "We are all connected and should express ourselves." Next, Zhang Tinggan, a representative of the people of the county who came to Shanghai to appeal, reported the truth of the incident and requested assistance. After discussion, the following was resolved: (1) County Magistrate Feng Peisan acted rashly and killed civilians, and a telegram should be sent to the National Government and the Jiangsu Provincial Government to remove him from his post and investigate him thoroughly. (2) Representatives should be elected to petition the National Government and the Jiangsu Provincial Government. (3) Representatives should be elected to return to Yangzhong to investigate the truth of the incident. (4) The public should be advised to wait quietly for a solution and not to riot. (5) County Magistrate Feng Peisan should be warned to act prudently and not to continue to act arbitrarily. (6) The media should be requested to uphold justice. The meeting adjourned after the resolutions.

Two Monks Actually Attempted Extortion - Monks Also Engage in Illegal Activities - Buddhist Scoundrels Commit a Truly Grave Sin 153

Rong Gengyuan, who resides at No. 24 Xiude Lane, Baike Road, works as a deputy buyer at the Kelai Zhen Cotton Yarn firm on Jiangxi Road. On the 19th of this month, Rong suddenly received a letter by mail. Upon opening it, the words inside were threatening and intended to extort five thousand silver dollars. It also instructed that the money be wrapped in old paper and sent to the trash can opposite the Chongfa Temple in Xisheng Lane on Gulou Road at 8 PM on the 20th, where someone would come to collect it. After receiving the letter, Rong reported it to the Xin Zha police station. Detective Yao Yuanlong, detectives Ruan Yao and Cui Shunke, and patrolmen Ye Yushan, Xia Yeshan, and Zong Weiting were dispatched to secretly guard the area around the lane. Before long, a monk was seen walking out of the Chongfa Temple on the opposite side. He went to the entrance of Xisheng Lane and looked at the trash can for a long time. He seemed to notice that there was nothing in the can, so he turned back to the temple. At that time, the detectives did not take any action because the monk did not make any move. The next day, Rong received a second threatening letter with even more intense language. It accused Rong of not following the instructions in the letter and warned that if he continued to disobey, appropriate measures would be taken. It also demanded that the money be sent to the front of Dr. Zhu Shaobo's office in Xisheng Lane the night before. Rong reported to the police again, and the same group of Chinese and foreign detectives was dispatched to lie in ambush at that location. At around 9 PM, the monk De Kuan (from Dongtai, Jiangbei, 27 years old) from the Chongfa Temple on the opposite side arrived. He first peered around suspiciously. Seeing that no one was there, he went straight to pick up a paper package that Rong had prepared and turned to flee. He was arrested by the detectives who stepped forward. At that moment, Wang Genrong was passing by the entrance of Xisheng Lane on Gulou Road, carrying a waste paper basket. The monk threw the paper package into the waste paper basket and was apprehended by the detectives. He was taken to the police station. Under questioning, De Kuan initially denied the charges, but later confessed that he had discussed the matter with the monk Anqing from the Chongfa Temple and that the draft was also written by Anqing. Chinese and foreign detectives immediately went to the Chongfa Temple and arrested Anqing. Several notes were found in De Kuan's room. These notes were compared with the threatening letter received by Rong, and the handwriting was found to be identical. They were ordered to be detained and were escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court yesterday morning. The police station's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, stated the facts of the case, saying that since the defendant's arrest, Rong Gengyuan had received another threatening letter. However, the police station had determined that the letter was mailed by the defendant De Kuan before his arrest. All the letters have been sent to the General Police Station and are being checked for handwriting, so they have not yet been submitted to the court. He requested a postponement to continue the investigation. Then, the witnesses Wang Genrong and Li He, a night watchman in Xisheng Lane, testified that they witnessed De Kuan picking up the paper package last night and throwing it into the waste paper basket upon seeing the detectives. De Kuan's statement was evasive, and Anqing also denied the charges, saying, "I have been a monk in Chongfa Temple for several years. De Kuan only arrived at the temple three or four months ago. We have no contact on weekdays. I know nothing about writing threatening letters." Judge Xue reviewed the confession and ordered the two defendants to be remanded in custody separately for further interrogation on the 30th.

Exploiting Children to Steal - Case Solved in Datong Sock Factory - Attention Should Be Paid to Abetting Masterminds 155

Recently, a class of rogue thieves has been discovered in the city who have had a unique idea of using copper coins, candy, food, etc. to entice ignorant children, mixing them into various shops, and using them to steal when people are unprepared. All stolen items are taken away by these people to be used. Because the shops are crowded with customers during business hours, they do not pay attention to these children, thinking they are brought by customers. As a result, many people have been victimized, and these thieves exploit children to steal. If they are exposed, they flee without a trace, making it difficult for the authorities to solve the cases. At around 2 PM yesterday afternoon, while business was bustling at the Datong Sock Factory at No. 49 Fangbang Road in the east of the city, two girls with bulging abdomens and panicked expressions were about to sneak out of the factory when they were discovered by factory workers, including Mei Zhiyou from Nanjing, who suspected their behavior. He immediately ordered them to stop and searched them, discovering two large skeins of wool yarn hidden in their clothes, causing their abdomens to bulge. At this point, Mei and others realized that the two girls were petty thieves and went outside to call for the police officer Wei Lianqing on duty. The two girls and the stolen goods were taken to the Second Precinct of the First District. During the preliminary interrogation by Chief Liu, Mei explained the situation, saying that various items had been stolen from the factory by children recently. He requested a thorough investigation. One girl confessed her name was Wang Mei, about eight years old, from Jiangbei, residing at No. 2 Tongfu Lane, Pudong. The other confessed her name was Gao Lanxiang, nine years old, also from Jiangbei, residing at No. 1 Hede Lane, Lan Mudu. They both stated that two men from Jiangbei had first used a lot of food to trick them into going to Puxi, then took them to the entrance of the Datong Sock Factory and forced them to go inside and steal the wool yarn placed on the counter. They had no choice but to go inside and, fortunately, were not noticed by the people in the factory. After stealing the wool yarn, they hid it on their bodies and were about to leave the factory when they were discovered and arrested by the people in the factory. The men who were standing outside the door monitoring their theft took the opportunity to flee. While confessing, the two girls cried and spoke in extreme remorse. They were ordered to be detained pending further investigation.

Executive Committee of the Chinese Children's Welfare Association - More Than Ten People Attended, Including Kong Xiangxi and Lin Kanghou - Resolved to Build a Sanatorium for Children with Lung Diseases 156

The Shanghai Chinese Children's Welfare Association held its 58th Executive Committee meeting yesterday afternoon at 1 PM at the Bankers' Association Clubhouse on Hong Kong Road.
