Spring and Autumn

Special Issue 丨Crab

Lament for Crabs 230

— 19

"The navel is round in September, pointed in October." Lake crabs are already on the market again. Iron cages are set up in front of wine shops or wild game stores. The gutless gentlemen in the cages are all foaming at the mouth, moving sideways and upwards, climbing non-stop, as if trying to escape; but because they don't have the strength of tigers or rhinos, they can only sigh softly. Speculating on their psychology: who doesn't have the hope of returning my freedom? And who doesn't have the desire to escape the invasion of foreign races 丨 humans 丨? However, their great enemy is moving their index finger, eager to satisfy their appetite. Then, the poor gentlemen can only surrender their lives without resistance.

Crabs move sideways, and they are cold-blooded. Because they move sideways, they can only dominate in their own circle. Because they are cold-blooded, their kind are tied up one by one by humans to be devoured, but they remain indifferent. Therefore, according to the principle of "survival of the fittest," crabs being eaten by humans is originally "self-inflicted, unpardonable," and there's no need for us 丨 humans 丨 to lament them. This refers to live crabs. As for dead crabs, logically, people should have a sense of pity and not use them as snacks. However, the dead crabs are still tied up tightly, lined up, with their white navels facing the sky, and no longer foaming or sighing softly. These kinds of dead crabs are naturally disdained by those who hold crabs and admire chrysanthemums; but those friends in short clothes have a predilection for scab eating. It is said that when a crab is about to die but not yet dead, its fat is still very thick. If you don't eat it at this time, when will you eat it! Moreover, dead crabs are always easier to subdue than live crabs. Live crabs still have two giant claws to defend themselves, and people can't help but be wary of them; now that they are about to die, their claws have also lost their ability to resist, and their fat can naturally be devoured. Therefore, comparing live crabs and dead crabs, it seems that dead crabs are more lamentable, especially those that are about to die.

I don't know why, every time I walk past a crab stall and see the live crabs in the cages and the dead crabs outside the cages, I always feel shocked and write Lament for Crabs.

Peculiarities of Crabs 231

— Jin Jie

Crab. In this season, whoever hears the word "crab" will be very excited, especially using crab as a topic. It can really be considered the most up-to-date article. However, what I am preparing to write here is not a study of blue backs, red claws, or 工-shaped patterns, nor is it anecdotes of famous people eating crabs after their deaths; but rather a few seemingly magical little stories, not self-deceiving myths!

One early morning in late autumn, at that time; I was not yet an adult, but I already knew the taste of crabs, so when the big crabs came on the market, I often followed the adults to hold crabs, drink wine, and have fun. One day, I and a few children went to a small river to play with boats. There happened to be someone setting up crab weirs in the river to catch crabs. We watched him catch the crabs that had been trapped in the weirs overnight, big and small, quite a few indeed; later, he suddenly caught a small group of three crabs connected together. Even after landing on the shore, they still did not separate. Not only did we all find it very strange, but even the crab catcher expressed great surprise. So he tried hard to separate them and found out that the middle crab was a cripple who had lost eight legs, so the two crabs next to it were carrying him in the river. At that time, my knowledge was limited, and I only felt it was fun, but now that I think about it, I can't help but admire the righteousness of the two crabs!

There is also a tenant in my family named Zhou Daxie, who is a famous strongman. When the villagers fight, whichever side he joins, that side is sure to win. It is said that he can kill a water buffalo with his bare hands and can also lift the stone railing by the well high up. I have never seen him kill a cow with my own eyes, but the scene of him lifting the well stone railing was indeed performed in front of me. At that time, I asked him why he had such great strength. He said: "Before I was sixteen, I was just an ordinary person. When I fought with others, I often ran away; in the autumn of that year, I went to Dongting Mountain and stayed at a friend's house. My friend was a fisherman, and he always made a living by catching crabs in the autumn. One night, I happened to be interested and went to work with him. I don't know how, but suddenly we caught a big crab that was bigger than a large flower bowl. Including the legs, the width must be more than two feet. As soon as I saw it, I was eager to eat it and begged my friend to leave it for me to drink with. My friend said that such a big crab might be harmful and advised me not to eat it. But I didn't see anything special about the crab, so I finally cooked it and ate it. Since then, my strength has increased unconsciously, especially my two arms." The above words were all said by Zhou Daxie himself and confirmed by others, but this guy later died silently and did not use his great strength in any way.

Crab Legs 232

— Shou Juan

The late calligrapher Li Meian, also known as Qing Daoren, loved crabs the most in his life. He could eat a hundred in one breath, and people called him Li Baixie (Li Hundred Crabs). This is the highest record for eating crabs.

Wu Guren, a poet of the Qing Dynasty, wrote a poem in Jianteng Xiaoji: "The crab sky knows the frost the earliest, the time after the oranges is yours, the old feelings can't help but be a little sour, when Wu Ji rubs it in her hand at the feast." The words "crab sky" are very new.

The late US President Harding died suddenly a few years ago. For a time, newspapers competed to report that he had been poisoned by crabs. Recently, someone wrote a book strongly arguing that it was not true, saying that his death had other reasons, which cannot be verified.

There are very few books about crabs. There were two in the Song Dynasty, one was Chuan Gong's Crab Manual, divided into two volumes, and the other was Gao Sisun's Xie Lue, with four volumes, describing it in the most detail. In the Tang Dynasty, there was a Crab Chronicle, written by the poet Chen Guimeng. After Chuan Gong, Chu Renhuo of the Qing Dynasty wrote Xu Xie Pu. These four gentlemen can be regarded as the confidants of the gutless gentleman.

The smallest type of crab is called the louse crab. The crab shell is only as big as an almond. Marinate it in good soy sauce and eat it the next day. The taste is very fresh and can be used as a snack.

Zhu Qigong, a famous scholar of the Qing Dynasty, loved crabs. One day, he was drinking and splitting crabs when a servant reported that a senior official had come to visit. Qigong scolded, "I won't exchange eight legs for a high official!" He continued to eat his crabs. The poet Li Zixiang gave him a poem with the line "Only call for turbid wine to pour on the madman, I am happy that the frost claw is better than a hot official," which was passed down as a good story at the time.

At the New World Amusement Park a few years ago, a beauty crab was displayed, which caused a sensation. The crab shell had a natural painting on it, like a peerless beauty, a different kind of crab.

Qiaodui Lu recorded: "There was an imperial censor who was inspecting Songjiang. The prefect, an old friend, invited him to drink, and jokingly gave him a couplet: 'The furnace fish has four gills, and one tail occupies Songjiang alone.' The prefect said: 'The crab has eight feet, and two claws move horizontally across the world.' The imperial censor knew that he was satirizing him, and laughed." How many people are there today who move horizontally across the world with their two claws?

The above are eight anecdotes in total, matching the number of crab legs.

Cooking Crabs 233

— Chen Liang

A string of crabs is hanging upside down. "Squeak, squeak" they are spitting white foam, the two little eyes are very small, the two claws are very big, and several crabs have become disabled, which is caused by the trampling of the people who catch and sell crabs, which makes me think of the wounded soldiers in the rear hospital. However, they and they are still a group waiting to be slaughtered.

Looking at their shape is quite pitiful. Their legs are constantly stretching, trying to struggle. I think of how free and unrestrained these little lives were when they were moving sideways in the sandy reed swamp. But now they are stranded and have to be put into the pot to be cooked one by one, and torn apart and eaten piece by piece.

I like to eat crabs but I can't bear to watch them being cooked.

The scene of cooking crabs will make people think of the embarrassment of those who are escaping from disasters.

First, live, fresh crabs are caught into the pot. The pot is cold, and the water is also cold. The crabs feel strange inside and crawl "squeak, squeak", but the water warms up little by little, and the crawling becomes tighter and more frequent, the steps to escape are chaotic, the water is hot, some climb halfway up the pot and then "cluck" slide down, the ones that slide down climb up again, climb up and slide down again... The "squeak, squeak" sound is sparse, and only the "gudu gudu" sound of boiling water is heard. Their lives are all over. When they are taken out of the pot, they are just a pile of corpses wearing blood-stained clothes.

There are also drunk crabs, which are anesthetized with wine and stuffed into jars. There are also flour paste crabs, which are beheaded by the cooks. They are eaten raw and skinned alive, suffering cruel torture. The small people in deep water and hot fire are no different from crabs. However, the people who cook crabs want to eat crabs, do the people who cook small people also want to prevent the small people from eating!

Elegant scholars who are holding crabs and admiring chrysanthemums, put down this glass of wine for a moment and listen to the groans of those in disaster.

Anecdotes About Crabs 234

— Bing Qian

After a few gusts of autumn wind and rain, the scenery of the suburbs is already drooping willows full of sorrow and maple leaves shaking red. The cries of crab sellers in the streets and alleys are endless, making people think of the elegant things of holding crabs and drinking wine.

The crabs in Beijing and Shanghai are best known for being produced in Yangcheng Lake, and the tenderness and deliciousness of the meat have long been well known. I teach in Wumen, which is close at hand. In fact, it should not be difficult to taste the delicacies, but the crabs on the market are cherished and self-regarded as rare goods, and each one costs one gold, which is not something that our humble teachers can afford. In addition, the students' papers are piled up on the table, and there is no time to enjoy the fun in time. In the midst of all kinds of boredom, let me tell a story about crabs as a way to satisfy my cravings without actually eating them!

The event took place during the Shunzhi period of the late Qing Dynasty. The protagonists were Zhang Yushu and County Magistrate Wu of Yanghu County丨now merged into Wujin County丨.

Zhang Yushu was a loyal, honest, and incorruptible prime minister who hated corrupt officials and bureaucrats the most in his life. In his later years, he retired to the Lin Garden and returned to his hometown of Zhenjiang, but he did not hold the principle of "not being in his position, not planning his affairs". He still often traveled incognito, disguised as a rural old man, to solve many injustices among the people. Therefore, local officials in the vicinity were a little bit apprehensive when they encountered this old man.

County Magistrate Wu of Yanghu, although only a ninth-rank official, was very powerful. He colluded with local gentry and oppressed the villagers. When this news reached the old man Zhang's ears, he disguised himself as a private school teacher and went to Yanghu to seek a teaching position. He was very good at giving guidance and was quite praised by the county magistrate. Before long, a grand banquet was held for the gentry in the office, and the old man Zhang was also among those invited. On this day, there was a lot of coming and going, and it was extremely prosperous. When it was time to take their seats, everyone pushed and shoved, and no one wanted to sit in the chief seat. Finally, they pushed it to Zhang Yushu, who was not polite at all. Everyone was not happy in their stomachs, and the sarcastic eyes all focused on the old man Zhang. The first dish was crab powder. Before the order to start eating was given, the teacher was asked to compose a poem about crabs. In their minds, they just wanted to tease him. The talented Zhang Yushu could just take the opportunity to express himself and said without thinking:

Eight feet are mixed and round.

Everyone heard this stupid and vulgar verse, and there was a great laughter like booing in the theater. Before the laughter had stopped, the second sentence came:

Who knows there is gold in the belly.

This was a bit sweet and aftertaste like eating olives. The last two sentences were said in one breath:

Two pincers push open the waves of the future,

What if Yanghu is ten thousand miles deep?

Everyone heard the implication, knew that it was the old man Zhang's trick, and prostrated themselves, not daring to look up. The old man Zhang gave them a great lesson and left the yamen without waiting for the end of the banquet.

When we are sitting and eating crabs, wouldn't it be more interesting to tell a story about crabs?

Shaoxing Crabs 235

— Ye Jufu

The most popular crabs in Shanghai are those from Yangcheng Lake. These crabs are large and plump, with slightly yellowish shells. It's said that the water in Yangcheng Lake is very clear, which is why the crabs from there are famous. But actually, the best crabs to eat are those from Shaoxing. The inland rivers of Shaoxing stretch 200 li from east to west and over 100 li from north to south. The former three counties of Shanyin, Kuaiji, and Xiaoshan encompass over 1,000 li, filled with large rivers and lakes. The freshness of the water is unmatched by any other place. The large crabs from Shaoxing have a deliciousness that can be described as the best in the country. Every year in late autumn, the fishermen in the inland villages build bamboo dams. On dark and windy nights, the "viscera-less gentlemen" (crabs) march sideways in groups. Round ones come first, followed by sideways ones. In each group, the round ones make up about eight or nine out of ten, while the long ones only make up one or two out of ten. Some say, "Crabs practice polygamy." The villagers, eager to taste the deliciousness, stay up all night, watching and waiting. After dusk, they come creeping and crawling. They never deviate from their path when crossing the dams. The villagers simply shine a light on them and catch them easily. They catch dozens at a time. Their shells are hard as iron. The next day, they buy a few catties of wine, boil the crabs, and feast on them. The crabs from Yangcheng Lake simply cannot compare.

When I was studying in Shaoxing as a child, I always had to eat "rice paddy crabs" (as the Shaoxing people call them) once a year. Three years ago, a relative returned from Guangdong to visit his family in Shaoxing and had already learned to drink alcohol. My relatives knew I liked this stuff, so they prepared a lot of dishes: fish, shrimp, meat, and especially the Shaoxing crabs, which I still remember with a very fresh and delicious aftertaste.

Basic Knowledge: Eating Crab Knowledge 236

— Yan Biguang

When the yellow chrysanthemums bloom and the red maple leaves are dyed, it is the time to hold crabs and drink wine. However, although crabs are delicious, they can be very harmful to a person's nutrition. Therefore, people who love crabs should understand the basic knowledge of eating crabs.

When choosing crabs for boiling, you must choose those with hard shells. The two large claws should be hairy, and the eight legs should be golden yellow. The hair on the legs should also be yellow. These crabs can be described as having rich roe and plump claws. If you encounter a crab with only one claw, or claws without hair, eating it can easily cause illness. To boil crabs, first wash the crabs clean with a hard-bristled brush, squeeze out the mud from the crab's eyes, and put a few grains of salt and a slice of ginger in the eyes. Tie them up with hemp rope, put some perilla leaves in the pot, and steam them. The taste will definitely be exceptionally delicious. ▲ Treatment for crab poisoning Because crabs are aquatic animals, they can destroy vitamins. People with weak constitutions are prone to poisoning after eating them. Most people who are poisoned suffer from abdominal pain. If you suffer from abdominal pain after eating crabs, you can eat a few coins' worth of longan meat to stop the pain and detoxify. Pregnant women must not eat crabs, as it may cause a miscarriage. This is because there is an abortifacient formula in traditional Chinese medicine called crab claw soup. Even if eating crabs does not necessarily cause everyone to miscarry, it is still too cold. Pregnant women should avoid eating many things, such as eating rabbit meat causing the child to have a cleft lip, and eating sparrow meat causing the child to be promiscuous.

To store fresh crabs so that they do not die and to make their meat and roe more plump and delicious, isn't that very difficult? I have a method. Use a small basket, fill it halfway with rice, put the fresh crab in, cover it with rice, and place it in a dark place. Take out the crab and cook it after half a year. The crab's belly will definitely have very beautiful roe oil, but the grains in the basket will have turned into empty shells. ▲ Crabs and persimmons are contradictory Crabs are cold, and persimmons are also cold. According to the Compendium of Materia Medica, crabs and persimmons are the most taboo. Those who violate this may die or become ill. I advise friends who eat crabs not to eat persimmons after eating crabs, and vice versa. Please do not play with your life!

▲ The medicinal effects of crabs When you are eating crabs, please do not forget! When separating the crab back from the crab belly, there is a crab "clothing" inside. Quickly take it off while it is still hot and rub it on places prone to frostbite in the cold winter. In winter, you will definitely be surprised why you didn't get frostbite this year! Gather the crab shells together, and in the summer, grind them into powder, mix them with wood shavings, and burn them to kill mosquitoes. It is very effective.

▲ The crab "monk" is a disease demon In the crab's shell, there is something that looks like a monk, with a slightly bitter and salty taste. Friends who eat crabs, quickly do not eat it, because eating it can easily lead to disease.

How to stew crab Crabs can be stewed. Wash the crab, put it in a bowl, add soy sauce, salt, good wine, and lard, and stew it on top of the rice cooker. It is good for drinking wine and eating rice, and it is very simple.

Financial: Bank of America Exchange Continues to Shrink, Benchmark Rises Another $8.40. Unfavorable US News Caused Initial Dip, Recovery Due to Silver Firms Seeking to Settle USD Exchange. 237

The gold market saw continuous appreciation of exchange rates due to stagnant US government gold buying prices, yet the trajectory over the half-day was convoluted, driven by overseas news. Exchange Market: Sterling Level, USD Tight, HSBC Listing Shows Sterling Up 125, USD Down 25 238

According to foreign telegrams yesterday, London large strips recently rose 1875 and far strips lengthened 125. USD silver shrank by half a point, forward silver prices dropped by 2 li. Free Talk

On Kicking Butts 260

— Lin Yutang

Chinese society has only two classes: those who kick other people's butts and those who prepare their butts to be kicked. Studying and going to school is the path to kicking other people's butts in the future. (See "Life" Magazine, Volume 1, Issue 1, "Da Sheng" article)

The same butt is more honored when kicked by a foreigner than by a compatriot. The same foot kicks harder when kicking a compatriot than when kicking a foreigner.

Those whose butts are kicked by foreigners often boast to those whose butts are kicked by compatriots. Those whose butts are kicked by compatriots often express admiration to those whose butts are kicked by foreigners, saying, "Why am I lagging behind?"

Slaves are best at offering their butts and are also best at kicking other people's butts once they gain power.

The Confucian concept of "positioning" is to tell those who kick butts to kick with confidence and those whose butts are kicked to accept it peacefully. But the idea of "peaceful acceptance" is always somewhat insufficient, so it must be supplemented by the Taoist concept of "being a ravine to the world," which involves both passive and active aspects. "Peaceful acceptance" is just that, passively waiting for a time when it is no longer necessary to be accepting, and it is not satisfaction. Being a ravine to the world, one's enduring virtue never leaves, because taking a lower position is seen as gaining power and having one's butt kicked is seen as a pleasure. Therefore, Chinese people believe in Confucianism when they are successful, seeing kicking others' butts as acting on behalf of heaven, and they believe in Lao-Zhuang when they are unsuccessful, seeing having their butts kicked as receiving from heaven. Thus, Chinese people deeply appreciate the beauty of the court when they are successful and deeply appreciate the beauty of the mountains and forests when they are unsuccessful.

When two children fight in an alley, the one with the bigger fist believes in Confucianism, and the one with the smaller fist believes in Taoism.

There is a genius for kicking butts and an inherent nature for offering butts. A genius who should be kicking other people's butts but suddenly encounters butts that refuse to be kicked has no room to display their talent and will inevitably scold the person in question. A person with an inherent nature to offer their butt in hopes of being kicked but cannot find an owner will inevitably drink wine and write poetry, lamenting their misfortune.

Those who kick others' butts usually want others to kick their own butts, as long as they believe that the other person has the status and good fortune to kick other people's butts. Yamen runners, low-level servants, gatekeepers, soldiers, politicians, and bureaucrats all simultaneously engage in kicking butts and offering butts.

In a country of ruler-ruler, minister-minister, father-father, and son-son, when the world is in order, the emperor kicks the empress's butt, the empress kicks the eunuch's butt, the eunuch kicks the minister's butt, the minister kicks the governor's butt, the governor kicks the prefect's butt, and the prefect kicks the commoner's butt. Assuming that everyone from the emperor to the commoner adheres to their position, follows the way without exceeding the bounds, and is kicked and kicks others, then the division of roles is defined, personal life is settled, the family is cultivated, the state is governed, and the world is at peace. When the world is out of order, the eunuch is kicked by the emperor and complains to the empress, and the empress kicks the emperor's butt instead. Thus, the superiors follow suit, and the commoner kicks the prefect's butt, the prefect kicks the governor's butt... This is called the decline of morality, great chaos in the world, the people rebel, and revolutionary parties appear.

Young people like to overthrow others and kick the butts of those who kick them. Older, more mature people do the opposite, showing restraint, because experience, knowledge, and worldliness tell them that rebelling against the kicker goes against heaven and often leads to a bloody end or, at the very least, a life of neglect. Submitting to the kicker is conforming to heaven, and conforming to heaven brings wealth, promotion, and a life of sitting on soft cushions and sofas.

When writers and politicians are unsuccessful, they often speak out on behalf of the small people whose butts are being kicked, arguing that butts should not be kicked, in accordance with the spirit of democracy. When they are successful, they argue that all butts should be kicked, in accordance with the aim of maintaining social order.

Scholars kick the butts of commoners, and soldiers then kick the butts of scholars. After writers and politicians come to power, they argue that all butts must be kicked by them, for the public good or for private gain, and they have no choice but to sacrifice themselves and serve the country. Soon, the soldiers kick them down and also praise, "That kick was well done!" But soon after, they argue that kicking butts violates the spirit of democracy.

There is a step in the process of moving from being kicked passively to kicking actively, called "touching." But anyone who touches Zhao Meng's butt will give Zhao Meng the right to kick their butt.

Those who like to kick butts are also distinguished by whether they cry out in pain when they are kicked. Those who are kicked and do not cry out in pain are said to be "restrained," while those who cry out in pain are said to "not know how to appreciate kindness." In China, a butt that is afraid of being kicked, or cries out in pain when kicked, can it still be considered a butt?

Spartan children also practiced not crying out in pain when their butts were beaten. But the situation is different from that in China. Spartans practiced not crying out in pain, not being kicked by the enemy, and at the same time practiced kicking back. Because the Spartans were brave and good at fighting, they were also good at kicking the butts of the Athenians. The philosophy of kicking butts has deeply penetrated the psychology of our people, and it will take a hundred years to eradicate it.

A Collection of Melodies and a Confucian Collection 261

— Yu Shixia

Literati in the Ming Dynasty were fond of melodies, and even pure Confucian scholars were fond of them. Wang Shouren would occasionally write a loose melody, and Qiu Jun devoted himself to writing legends, with four types: Five Relationships Complete, Throwing the Pen, Lifting the Tripod, and Luo Nang. Some criticized him for being a great Confucian scholar and should not pay attention to operas, but he regarded them as enemies. One day, he passed a temple and saw a story painted on the walls. He couldn't help but be surprised and asked a monk, "How could there be this in an empty door?" The monk replied, "The old monk enlightened to Zen here." The Confucian scholar used opera to preach, and the old monk enlightened to Zen from The Romance of the Western Chamber. This is truly worthy of exclamation. Jiao Xun's Play Theory says, "According to legend, at the end of the Hongzhi period of the Ming Dynasty, a certain professor of the Quanzhou Prefecture School, a native of Nanhai, was quite aloof. One day, he held a banquet in the Minglun Hall and performed The Romance of the Western Chamber. The next day, an anonymous person wrote a couplet on the school gate, 'Unhappy for literature, the Nanhai gentleman came to the Minglun Hall; the school has no light, the Romance of the Western Chamber was performed in the professor's hall.' When he came out and saw it, he was ashamed and his old ways disappeared." Was it only the Confucian scholars who did this? Even the classical Chinese style of writing, which carries the Dao, was fond of The Romance of the Western Chamber. The same book also says: "Tang Jingchuan wrote after being half drunk. First, he sang the passage from The Romance of the Western Chamber in which Huiming did not recite the Lotus Sutra, danced and stretched out paper to write, and the text was completed. See Sixteen Views on Writing". Even those who call themselves disciples of the sage are like this, so it is no wonder that other literati are fond of music, whether it is only for enjoyment or creation. The Ming government was harsh and there were many taboos. Hiding in opera was also a way for literati to avoid disaster, and the opera was very prosperous in the Ming Dynasty. Lu Tiancheng's preface to Melody Grades says, "I liked melodies when I was dancing as a child, and I liked filling in lyrics when I was weak. Every time I went to the market and saw a legend, I would take it home, and my basket gradually filled up. At first, I wanted to build a collection of melodies, from the creations of talented predecessors to the compilations of corrupt Confucian scholars, and collect them all, making a grand view of the rivers and seas. But then I said that there were too many to collect, and the compilations would soil my collection, so I lost them one by one." It is a pity that no one in the Ming Dynasty was willing to create a collection of melodies. Otherwise, Wu Mei, Zheng Zhenduo and others today would not have to exhaust their efforts in searching for lost melodies. How can one boast of quantity and compete for knowledge?

Cao Xueqin of the Ming Dynasty once said that the two families of Taoism and Buddhism have collections, so why don't we Confucian scholars have them? He wanted to create a Confucian collection to stand alongside the Taoist and Buddhist collections. Therefore, he collected books from the Siku Quanshu and divided them into categories. After more than ten years, the work was not completed and the two capitals were lost. It is a pity that the Confucian collection was never completed. Otherwise, to this day, the Taoist and Buddhist collections have been published, and now the rare books of the Siku Quanshu are being reprinted. It can be seen that the disciples of the sage have not disappeared, and that the inherent culture is waiting to be explained. How do we know that no one will reprint the Confucian collection?

In Harbin 262

— Li Huiying

By an unexpected chance, I met three people who split wood.

Originally, in the streets of Harbin, there were many people like them. They were always in groups of three or four, carrying axes and saws, soliciting business, splitting wood for people.

They walked the streets every day, only fearing that rainy days were their days of rest.

The three people I knew were all from Shandong. In fact, only Shandong people could do such heavy work. No matter how others called them coolies, I respected them as the "pillars of society."

Afterwards, every day at the same time, I would see them three, walking at a sparse pace, carrying axes and saws, appearing on the street where I lived. They would greet each other, and they all had an unspeakable joy. I saw that they were somewhat different from others, but I couldn't say what it was. Because of this, it aroused my concern and affection for them.

We became close friends, and we talked about things that only close friends could talk about. They knew that I was a young student who had returned to the north from the south. Although they didn't know what I did, they worried about me. They sincerely advised me to be very careful when speaking to outsiders, because there were as many secret agents in the city as ants on the ground. At the same time, they honestly and sincerely told me about their past, so that I knew that a year ago they were farmers from the Fujin area of ​​the Lower River, with many people in their families. Later, they joined a gang and became guerrillas. Later, they were scattered, but they did not easily forget that scattering. That was the most fierce bloody battle between them and the Japanese soldiers, with more than 2,000 people, when the Japanese soldiers truly died more than 200 people under their blades. Later, a great flood occurred in the river. After the flood, there was no food to eat, no houses to live in, and no land to cultivate, so they came to this city to seek a life.

At that time, I asked:

"Why don't you do it again?"

They didn't answer me, just looked at me and smiled. I knew there was a hidden story in this, so I changed the subject.

In the streets of Harbin, especially in the Nangang and Majiagou areas, some streets often extend from all directions and intersect at one place, and then they go to different places. There will inevitably be a small garden at the intersection, with ancient plums planted and benches placed in the shade of the trees. Every day at noon, unable to withstand the scorching heat, I would take a paper fan and go to that kind of place to escape the heat. Sitting on the bench, I would accept the cool breeze blowing from all the street entrances; I would listen to the little birds singing in the treetops; the lazy sound of horses' hooves and the rumbling of big cars on the street allowed me to find tranquility in the hustle and bustle. After a while, I would unknowingly lie down on the bench and fall asleep.

That day, at the same time, I went to the shade of the trees to escape the heat again. After sitting down, I suddenly remembered that I hadn't seen my three close friends for several days. But then I thought: Maybe they went to "Daoli," "Daowai," or those places in Majiagou to solicit business.

However, I was wrong after all. One day in the evening, when I had just walked to the trolleybus, I saw a group of prisoners walking in front of me, under police surveillance, wearing handcuffs. They looked like just some coolies. What crimes could they have committed? But suddenly, I saw them three in the crowd! After not seeing you for a few days, you have committed illegal things? I thought.

From the discussions of the people watching the excitement on the roadside, I learned that they were all criminals who had been arrested for "endangering the new country." They were plainclothes soldiers of the volunteer army, planning to riot in the city. Originally, these irresponsible words could be ignored, but at this moment, I felt that it was almost the same, because I remembered the differences between my three friends and others, and their past of not answering my questions and just smiling at me. This is naturally a serious issue, but I hope they regain their freedom soon.

They also saw me, with that kind of laughter full on their faces, which probably only true anti-Japanese soldiers who are not afraid of death can have.

I smiled back at them, a bitter smile more bitter than coptis chinensis.

Small Satires 263

— Written by Thoreau, Translated by Shi Heng

(1) Speculation with Pebbles

In the town there was a road covered in pebbles. A passing car kicked one of the pebbles out. This pebble spoke to itself: "Why should I be stuck here tightly squeezed among many of my kind? I would rather live alone."

A child passed by and picked up the pebble.

The pebble thought in its heart, "I want to travel, so I will travel. All I need is a strong and full desire."

The child threw it towards a house. The pebble thought again, "I want to fly, so I will fly. It's very simple - I just need to wish it so."

With a "bang," the pebble went through a glass window. The glass shattered, and cried out:

"Oh, you wicked thing! What are you doing?"

But the pebble replied:

"If you had given way in advance, this wouldn't have happened. I don't want anyone blocking my way. Everything must be arranged for my benefit - that's my motto."

The pebble landed on a soft bed and thought, "I've been flying for a while, now I want to rest for a bit."

A servant came in, picked the pebble up from the bed, and threw it back out the window, so it was lying on the pebble road again.

So the pebble cried out to its kind: "Brothers, how are you? I just visited a mansion, but I don't like the nobles at all. My heart yearns for the masses, so I'm back again."

Two Brothers (40) 264

— By Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

So, this young, free, wealthy man, prepared to dedicate himself to all tender Marias, one day happened to walk into a small shop, perhaps noticing the beautiful shopkeeper. He bought something. He came again later. He started chatting with them, becoming more familiar day by day. He often came to buy something, so as to have the right to sit in their house, laugh with the young woman, and shake hands with her husband.

And then… and then… ah! Heavens… and then…?

He had loved and caressed the first child, the jeweler's child, and when the other child was born, he kept his secret silent until death. Then, his grave was sealed, his flesh decayed, his name was no longer mentioned, and he disappeared forever. He no longer needed to worry, fear, or hide, and he left all his property to the second child! … Why? … He was a clever man… he should have understood and anticipated that he would almost inevitably lead people to suspect that this child was his. Then wasn't he ruining a woman's reputation? If Zhean wasn't his son, how could he have done such a thing?

Suddenly, a clear, horrifying memory surfaced in Pierre's mind. Maria had golden hair, and Zhean also had golden hair. He now remembered a small portrait he had seen when he lived in Paris, placed on the mantelpiece in the living room. This portrait was now gone. Where had it gone? Was it lost, or hidden? Ah! If only he could hold it in his hand for a second! Perhaps his mother had hidden it in a secret drawer, the kind specifically for keeping love tokens.

Thinking about this, he became extremely agitated and involuntarily let out a sigh, a short sigh forced out by intense pain. Suddenly, the sirens on the embankment, as if hearing his sigh, as if understanding his sigh and responding to it, roared beside him. This supernatural monster's cry, louder than thunder, this roar that could overwhelm the sound of the wind and the waves, spread through the darkness of the invisible sea shrouded in fog.

Then, similar sounds, through the fog, from near and far, rose again from the darkness. These cries emitted by blind ocean liners sounded terrifying.

Then everything was silent again.

Pierre opened his eyes and looked around, surprised that he was in that place. He had awakened from a nightmare.

"I'm crazy, I'm suspecting my mother," he lamented. Then his heart was filled with filial piety, emotion, regret, prayer, and sorrow. His mother! He understood her now as he always had. How could he doubt her? Wasn't the soul and life of this simple, chaste, upright woman clearer than water? Who, having seen and known her, could not think that she was beyond suspicion? And now it was he, her son, who was doubting her! If he could take her into his arms at that moment, how he would hug and kiss her, comfort her, how he would kneel before her and beg her forgiveness!

Special Issue on Basic English Studies: Understanding Basic English 265

— Gong Pu

Shanghai is one of the largest international commercial centers in the world today. The application of foreign languages is more urgent and necessary here than in any other place in China. Among foreign languages, English is the most fashionable, so there are more people learning English than any other foreign language, which is a natural phenomenon. However, although the need for English is urgent, the difficulties and time required to learn English cannot be reduced. This is the most difficult thing for beginners, especially those who only have the opportunity to learn English as adults. Suddenly, we hear about the invention of Basic English, which only requires learning 850 words to handle ordinary conversations. This should be a happy thing for friends who have wanted to learn English but don't have a lot of time and money to spend. Who knew that this excessive expectation would soon be greatly disappointed, because the number of words in Basic English is too small to handle even ordinary elementary school conversations. Using it to handle complex commercial Q&A will naturally be full of jokes and not be considered language. At the same time, a group of teachers who speak English well launched a major attack, using sarcasm and abuse to the extreme. As a result, many people who urgently wanted to learn English were disappointed, and the promoters were inevitably discouraged. Because this publication has received many articles discussing this issue, and many readers have written to request answers to this question, although this publication has previously published several articles, there are still many manuscripts in storage. Therefore, it was decided to publish this special issue. But our attitude is impartial. We will publish all the submitted articles as much as possible without prejudice, hoping that readers can understand this.

In the text of this special issue, there is no doubt that critical arguments occupy an absolute majority. The reporter has stated in advance that he does not want to take sides, so he will not participate in any opinions. However, I deeply feel that there is one point we should recognize about Basic English, that English is still one of the most universally applicable languages among foreign languages in the world today. Let's put aside the nationality of Basic English and only talk about the purpose of the inventor of Basic English. I think at least part of it is to reduce the difficulty of learning English and to use the existing position of English for more widespread application. This motive is what we should understand. Because to learn a language, you must have opportunities to practice it often, so that it is not easy to forget. English at least occupies a superior position in this respect, and Basic English is nothing more than a product based on this point. To be fair, the biggest shortcoming of Basic English is that there are too few words. If the inventor can revise and supplement it based on facts, then its future is still unlimited. We hope that readers will not completely dismiss its value because of the harshness of the critics. You should know that when a new thing comes out, severe criticism is always unavoidable. But its final victory depends entirely on whether the inventor and those who sympathize with it can humbly accept criticism, examine the opinions of the critics, and improve it. This is the general principle of creating a new business. We should also use this as a basis for predicting the future of Basic English.

Finally, the reporter has one more suggestion to the inventor of Basic English, that I deeply believe that even if the number of words in Basic English becomes "1850 words," it is still easy to learn and can still be called Basic English. Then, I think the jokes will be much less than with "850 words."

A General Discussion of the Structure of Basic English 266

— Shi An

What exactly is Basic English? This is what I want to study with the readers of this publication now.

First, Basic English is not something that can be easily learned in a few months, as some people say. Its shortcomings are exactly the same as those of Standard English. For example, troublesome spelling, irregular verb conjugations, and unreasonable idioms are all copied directly from Standard English. These points are the most difficult for learners in Standard English. It is clearly impossible to say that they will suddenly become easier in Basic English.

Second, Basic English is full of weirdness and clumsiness, and it does not conform to the rules of language at all. Part of its content is completely different from Standard English, which is what Ogden and others boast about as the characteristic of Basic English, but it is also the most difficult and lacking part of it. This is because many words that are necessary in our daily life are discarded, leaving only 850 words to take on the functions of thousands of words. There are more than dozens of the most basic and common human actions every day, from getting up to going to bed, but Basic English only has eighteen verbs. Therefore, when you run, you can't say "run" (Run), you can only say "go quickly" (Go Quickly); to shave, you can only say "take away the hair on the face." This kind of statement fully exposes the poverty of expression. Just imagine, if you learn Basic English and you can't even distinguish between running and walking, and you can't shave clearly, how can you handle negotiations with others properly? If you use Basic English to express your thoughts, can you be sure that you will not be misunderstood?

The content of human life and the interaction between people are becoming richer and more complex day by day, adapting to the development of social productivity. Since the scope of our activities is getting larger, the language used to express thoughts also becomes richer to meet practical needs. Basic English only leaves us with eighteen verbs, which is to make the language regress from rich to poor, clearly violating the law of language evolution and engaging in an act of reversing the language.

Furthermore, nouns are even more difficult to remember and clumsy. Language is a tool for humans to communicate thoughts, so its most basic condition is that people understand it when it is spoken. If only you understand it, then it is not human speech. In Basic English, there are most of the words that are very incomprehensible and only you can understand. For example, Standard English says that an onion is Onion, which is very simple and clear, but Basic English simply doesn't want it, and insists on using "a white root that makes the eyes water" instead. This kind of roundabout talk is not liked by the British themselves (please refer to the British criticism of Basic English in the Daily International Anthology).

Announcement from this Publication 267

Since this publication published several articles on Basic English and Esperanto studies in previous issues, we have recently received many manuscripts of the same nature, while manuscripts of other natures are very scarce. Therefore, in addition to publishing a "Special Issue on Basic English Studies" in this issue, we plan to publish a "Special Issue on Esperanto Studies" in the next issue. We hereby announce this in advance.

Chinese people who learn ordinary English also "hate" it very much (see Mr. Lin Yutang's article), because it is very difficult to remember and easy to misunderstand. An onion is indeed "a white root that makes the eyes water," and the "spicy vegetable" commonly seen in our villages is also a genuine "white root" that can also "make the eyes water." This kind of heaven-knows gibberish is simply not qualified to be a language.

Roundabout speech is the specialty of people with a low degree of change and small talk. When people in the countryside of the interior see a car for the first time, they say it is "something with four round feet running and roaring": children who don't understand glasses say "circles on the eyes." So Basic English is not a new invention of Ogden, but just learning from children and people with very low cultural standards, imitating their way of expressing thoughts.

methods of expressing thoughts. However, after seeing "something with four round feet running and roaring" twice, people in the interior countryside gradually know to call it "car." Once told by their fathers or mothers, children will also call a circle on the eyes "glasses." But our Chinese scholars and editors are still reversing the trend, treating barbaric expressions as rare commodities and considering them a new invention of the twentieth century. Isn't this a joke?

Talking About the Characteristics of Basic English Grammar 268

— Qin Shiyin

According to page 130 of "Introduction," the grammar of Basic English has two characteristics, namely: (1) Other national languages (including ordinary English) all have lengthy verb conjugation tables. These changes cannot be learned well in a few years. Basic English only needs to memorize one verb conjugation table. (2) Even Esperanto, which is most supported, has at least 500 rules for the endings of related words. Basic English is not like that. But if we know that the total number of rules in "Esperanto" Esperanto is only sixteen, and only the sixth rule talks about verb changes, it is more reasonable and simpler than the verb conjugation table of Basic English.

The compound nouns and prefixes and suffixes, which are exclaimed by the promoters of Chinese Basic English as the most ingenious features, are actually shallow and poor.

The so-called compound nouns are either formed by the combination of two nouns, or by the combination of a noun and a direction noun, always limited to those in Standard English (see page 31 of "Grammar"). In this way, it is limited to 600 nouns and 20 direction nouns (prepositions). Although some other types of words can exceptionally be joined together in pairs to form a new word, its meaning is completely new and cannot be known at a glance (see page 102 of "Introduction"). In Esperanto, all words can be combined with each other to form new words, as long as they are logical, called combined words.

As for prefixes, in Basic English, most of the fifty adjectives of nature use un to express the meaning of "opposite" (see page 65 of "Grammar"). The twenty prepositions of Basic English can also be used as quasi-prefixes and added before ten simple verbs to form new verbs (see page 75 of "Introduction"). But this is such a narrow range. Not only have the 850 words already taken away the lively life of prefixes, but the number of prefixes is simply too small. In Esperanto, there are nine prefixes, forty quasi-prefixes, one special prefix, and five other prefixes in academia, so that the vocabulary does not have to be clumsily, unscientifically, and anti-evolutionarily limited to 850 words and can be lively improved. For example, if the prefix in Esperanto that expresses the meaning of "opposite" is mal, then in the twenty-five pairs of opposite adjectives on page 3617 of "Introduction," a large part of them would not need to use words with completely different forms in Esperanto.

There are only four things in Basic English that can barely be called suffixes: er·or·ing·ed. In fact, or is an exception of er, and adding ing can be transformed into a noun, or it can be used as an adjective, just like ed, which is just the ending of a grammatical part of speech. However, the classification of parts of speech in Esperanto is clearly stipulated with endings, so that there will be no confusion like the two Buildings in Abuilderisbuildingabuilding. Although it is easy to distinguish in this simplest sentence, Esperanto has twenty-nine suffixes, four quasi-suffixes, six special suffixes, and sixteen suffixes in academia. This makes it possible for Esperanto to achieve the goal of reducing the vocabulary and making the language "simplified" and, more importantly, rationalized without violating the principle of the evolution of language and society towards richness and arrogantly limiting the number of words.

Therefore, no matter how beautifully Basic English is said by some people, it is not as rational and simplified as Esperanto. I think that the promoters of Chinese Basic English should always believe that reducing the vocabulary cannot be achieved by mechanically reducing the number and using the "circumlocution method" (which is actually the method of memorizing dictionaries).

Scientific Language 丨 Basic English 269

— Zhang Guoquan

The development of natural science has shrunk space. In international transportation, we have trains, ships, and even airplanes. But in the spiritual communication of mankind, we still lack a tool. Well, now an international language has appeared, that is, "Basic English," the new invention of Professor Ogden, a language expert at Cambridge University in England!

We all know that English is almost universally spoken, just like the British flag, especially in China and other places in the East. Therefore, adopting English as an international language is really the most appropriate and convenient way. However, English is very difficult to learn, so it is impossible to ask people from all countries to learn English. Professor Ogden saw this point, so he vowed to engage in the work of internationalizing and simplifying English. It took him ten years of hard work to select 850 words from Standard English. It can be seen that this is the crystallization of science.

Because Basic English only has 850 words, it is very easy to learn and can be successful in three months. After learning it, you can speak, write, and write letters, and you can do everything. If you want to study further, you can also use this to study Standard English, so it is also a shortcut to learning Standard English.

This is a newly invented international language. There are still shortcomings in theory and content, but it can be gradually improved. And now there are already more than thirty kinds of Basic English books in the world, and six have been published in China. We can imagine that the number of people learning Basic English all over the world will slowly increase.

The characteristic of Basic English is that it can express everything with a small number of words. However, it is originally impossible to contain all the necessary words in 850 words. Therefore, in Basic English, ten or fewer words are used to explain it. This is the most ingenious part of its organization.

Now, everyone feels the need for an international language. And this Basic English is the best international language. Even if you want to learn English, you should start with Basic English.

On the Practicality of Basic English 270

— Deng Liren

The promoters of Basic English claim that the 850 words of Basic English "can be used to write or say everything that is necessary in daily life." But how can these mere 850 words express everything in daily life? Therefore, we have to use the method of compiling a dictionary to "explain" the words outside of these 850. But for the person who compiles the dictionary, the purpose is originally to "explain" the meaning of the word. In order to make the meaning of the word clear, it is originally necessary to use dozens or even hundreds of words to "explain" a word. Since Basic English is a kind of language, then the purpose of language is naturally to be able to express one's own meaning smoothly and to be correctly understood by others. The purpose of language is definitely not to "explain," definitely not to compile a dictionary. But Basic English forces people to speak in the tone of compiling a dictionary, which is obviously wrong. When writing an article, if you encounter a word outside of the 850, Ogden teaches us to use footnotes, but when speaking, how do you use footnotes? For example, when we use Basic English to make a phone call, if we encounter a word that is not in the 850, can we say: "Sorry, wait a moment, let me first add a footnote! " And everyone has to carry a pocket-sized "Basic English Dictionary" with them, whether eating or defecating, so that they can look up the footnotes they want at any time. Otherwise, there is a risk of hitting a wall at any time. Moreover, this Basic English dictionary, according to the promoters of Chinese Basic English, only has 7,500 words, in other words, only 7,500 "explanations." Then, if you encounter a word outside of the 7,500 (whoever is born into the world will inevitably have this time), how do you "explain" it? Ogden has no way to instruct us, probably "still under study." Never mind, let's leave this point alone. Let's try to see the practicality of this language.

If there is a waiter in a restaurant who is learning Basic English, or a servant in a foreigner's house, he will have to stop doing business with his master sooner or later. Because not only is "onion" "a white root that makes the eyes water," but "waxberry cake" also has to be said to be "a bluish-yellow berry with hair on the skin covered with batter." "Fried flatfish" is called "flatfish with a delicate taste, cooked in oil on the fire." "Cabbage" also has to be said to be "a green plant with a round heart or head." This kind of statement is not only difficult to remember, but no one in the vegetable market or food store will understand it.

If there is a nurse among those who are learning Basic English, her fate is similar to that of the servant. When going out to see a doctor with the doctor, the doctor wants "a kind of pointed tube with a pusher-puller, using air pressure to release water into it, and then release it into a very thin line of water, for medical use." This is the meaning of a "syringe" for injections. Who can remember it exactly? And whether this nurse will be kicked out by the doctor is something we can imagine.

If it is an apprentice in a store, then the difficulties he encounters will be even greater. Not only are there no commonly used words such as "telephone" in the 850 words, which must be learned separately, but when he meets customers, he cannot even say "sir" or "madam" (which are not in the 850 words), and can only directly call them "that man" or "that woman."

Although we are not prophets (according to the tone of Basic English, we should say: "people who talk about future things"), we can guess that Basic English will never
